    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

<span id="freeTextContainer13497425717690840336">De vrolijke oude koning van het goede land Katoren is overleden zonder een opvolger te hebben. Zes zure ministers regeren het land en beweren al 17 jaar dat ze een nieuwe koning zoeken, maar er gebeurt niets. Dan komt de 17-jarige Stach de ministers vragen wat je moet doen om koning te worden. De ministers geven Stach zeven bijna onuitvoerbare opdrachten, waarop al velen v</span>
  <span id="freeText13497425717690840336" style="display:none">De vrolijke oude koning van het goede land Katoren is overleden zonder een opvolger te hebben. Zes zure ministers regeren het land en beweren al 17 jaar dat ze een nieuwe koning zoeken, maar er gebeurt niets. Dan komt de 17-jarige Stach de ministers vragen wat je moet doen om koning te worden. De ministers geven Stach zeven bijna onuitvoerbare opdrachten, waarop al velen voor hem hun kracht beproefd hebben. Maar Stach is niet bang. Hij is slim en weet met gezond verstand alle opdrachten uit te voeren, waardoor hij Katoren weer tot een leefbaar land maakt. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13497425717690840336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I found a list of translations. It includes the English and French translation: "How To Become King" (1971) and "Chevalier de l'impossible" (1975). I <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I found a list of translations. It includes the English and French translation: "How To Become King" (1971) and "Chevalier de l'impossible" (1975). I don't know whether they are still available, but I hope you can find them. It is really worth reading!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer504953165" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12617452291653063092">This book has been the topic of many arguments at our home, and they usually went like this:<br/><br/>Mother: 'Please pick another book, we've read this four times already. It must be boring by now. Pick another.'<br/>Me, my brother and sister: 'NOOOOO! Read this! We want to hear about Stach!'<br/><br/>We usually won, of course, because my mum was grateful she'd found a book all three of us liked and we were still eager to hear about dragons, moving churches, screeching birds and a brave young boy who wanted to be king.</span>
  <span id="freeText12617452291653063092" style="display:none">This book has been the topic of many arguments at our home, and they usually went like this:<br /><br />Mother: 'Please pick another book, we've read this four times already. It must be boring by now. Pick another.'<br />Me, my brother and sister: 'NOOOOO! Read this! We want to hear about Stach!'<br /><br />We usually won, of course, because my mum was grateful she'd found a book all three of us liked and we were still eager to hear about dragons, moving churches, screeching birds and a brave young boy who wanted to be king.<br />It's a brilliant work of Children's literature, with a good plot, morals and lovely characters.<br />You follow Stach on his journey across the Kingdom in order to complete seven assignments, one in every part. Only if he completes them all, will he be crowned the new King. You will meet all his new friends, the mayors, the wifes, the commoners, as well as his enemies and the sly ministers who crave power of their own. Join Stach as he completes assignment after assignment, finds his future Queen and hold your beath when he finally makes that ultimate leap of faith. And find out whether it's been worth it, in the end.<br /><br />A story that will make even the reluctant boy/girl read and can capture the imagination of a wide audience. A story to treasure. <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3212059504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15205777204957311946">The King of Katoren is a prize winning Dutch children's book first published in 1971. The story is of the 17 (but eventually 18<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ sorry about the spoiler <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) year old hero attempting to complete a series of tasks, not Herculean ones as they are generally less savage, in order to become King of the fictional kingdom of Katoren.<br/><br/>The hero is a relative of a typical archetypal hero who succeeds through being modest and kindly, he is not exactly true to this type - he is not </span>
  <span id="freeText15205777204957311946" style="display:none">The King of Katoren is a prize winning Dutch children's book first published in 1971. The story is of the 17 (but eventually 18<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ sorry about the spoiler <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) year old hero attempting to complete a series of tasks, not Herculean ones as they are generally less savage, in order to become King of the fictional kingdom of Katoren.<br /><br />The hero is a relative of a typical archetypal hero who succeeds through being modest and kindly, he is not exactly true to this type - he is not aided by any small animals that he saves or aids for instance, but he is broadly similar in being fairly innocent, lacking any intrinsic advantage in his quest and having nothing to aid him on his way beyond his native wit and preparedness to talk <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and shockingly, listen <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> to the various people that he meets.<br /><br />The Dutch seemed to me far simpler than in the translation of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13023.Alice_in_Wonderland" title="Alice in Wonderland by Lewis Carroll" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice in Wonderland</a> that I read, and I was able to follow the story, though on a second reading, checking a few words with a dictionary might possibly be a good idea.<br /><br />I was interested that it combined elements of a contemporary (for 1971) setting, such as newspapers, railways, and the radio with fantastical elements such as a dragon, I felt too that the way that the hero picks up a girlfriend and how the relationship is developed <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ in an entirely 'clean' manner I hasten to reassure the most modest readers  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was different from how equivalent relationships were handled in English language children's books - specifically that it was entirely relaxed and accepting.<br />3rd march 2020</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7330744120903421038">*Short English Review Below*<br/><br/>Dit is echt een van de klassiekers van de Nederlandse jeugdboeken. Ik ken niet veel mensen (van mijn generatie althans; begin jaren 90 geboren) die hem niet gelezen hebben. Ik vond het vroeger ook een heel spannend en leuk verhaal. Het blijft een leuk boek. Een van mijn favoriete kinderboeken!<br/><br/>~<br/><br/>The King of Katoren dies without leaving an heir and a group of ministers seizes the power, being very reluctant to give it away to the new king, should he arise.   <span id="freeText7330744120903421038" style="display:none">*Short English Review Below*<br /><br />Dit is echt een van de klassiekers van de Nederlandse jeugdboeken. Ik ken niet veel mensen (van mijn generatie althans; begin jaren 90 geboren) die hem niet gelezen hebben. Ik vond het vroeger ook een heel spannend en leuk verhaal. Het blijft een leuk boek. Een van mijn favoriete kinderboeken!<br /><br />~<br /><br />The King of Katoren dies without leaving an heir and a group of ministers seizes the power, being very reluctant to give it away to the new king, should he arise. Therefore, they set a set of seven nearly impossible (almost Herculean) works that need to be completed...<br /><br />I really liked this story as a child. It's a real classic in The Netherlands and I think almost everyone has read it at some point. I cannot vouch for the English translation, since I haven't read it, but I would certainly recommend the Dutch version. It was one of my favorites. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6006000-melanie?shelf=the-netherlands">the-netherlands</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6006000-melanie?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6006000-melanie?shelf=more-than-once">more-than-once</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196922943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4368141962984436986">Reread April 5, 2014. Still fun^^! A lot shorter than I remember though... but then, I was quite a bit younger when I last read it.<br/> <br/>_______________________________<br/><br/><b> Original review: </b><br/><br/>One of my all-time favourite (Dutch) children's books! <br/><br/>The story follows Stach (not sure if this is his English name also), a smart and bold (sometimes just slightly short of insolent, but in a charming way) young man who sets out to complete seven impossible tasks in seven cities to prove that he is worthy of becomin</span>
  <span id="freeText4368141962984436986" style="display:none">Reread April 5, 2014. Still fun^^! A lot shorter than I remember though... but then, I was quite a bit younger when I last read it.<br /> <br />_______________________________<br /><br /><b> Original review: </b><br /><br />One of my all-time favourite (Dutch) children's books! <br /><br />The story follows Stach (not sure if this is his English name also), a smart and bold (sometimes just slightly short of insolent, but in a charming way) young man who sets out to complete seven impossible tasks in seven cities to prove that he is worthy of becoming the king of Katoren. <br /><br />First of all, I could not help but love Stach! I love the way he tackles each of these problems using his wits and astute powers of observation, a creative mind and a healthy dose of common sense, and how he isn't wowed into silence by shows of authority or threats but just keeps going until he solves the problem and makes people see some sense. I also love his personality, and how he shows all of his qualities, such as kindness, intelligence, courage, self-sacrifice and a useful streak of stubbornness and persistance, without it becoming too obvious or moralistic. Furthermore this book has many more amazing characters, most of them interesting and well-rounded and in some way or another managing to avoid the black-and-white good-bad divide that I have encountered in other children's books. <br /><br />Each of the cities in this book is plagued with a specific problem, most of them reflecting and criticising (then) current problems of society (pollution, religious conflict, production of weapons) and attitudes of people (greed, pettiness, complacency). This adds an extra layer for the reader to contemplate on, and fortunately it is never done too heavy-handedly but manages to give an airy and imaginative twist to some well-known and sometimes over-debated issues. <br /><br />All in all this is just an incredible feel-good story, it is smart and funny, and has enough depth to have readers visit it again and again without it ever getting old!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4368141962984436986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SYqj8zxQgV8P5gtAoym5x96NzeC9uS0jDMlcMmO3CM2dfdE921WGS8tGHTyLVNOHMjXItml2nA1Ih0OnxBpJag==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1336126482328383652">Na de middelbare school studeerde Jan Terlouw wis- en natuurkunde in Utrecht en deed vervolgens 13 jaar onderzoek in de natuurkunde, in Nederland, de Verenigde Staten en Zweden. Daarna ging hij in de politiek. In 1971 kwam hij voor D'66 in de Tweede Kamer. Twee jaar later werd hij voorzitter van de Tweede Kamer-fractie. Onder zijn leiding kwam D'66 uit een diep dal, en behaalde het in 1981 een gro</span>
  <span id="freeText1336126482328383652" style="display:none">Na de middelbare school studeerde Jan Terlouw wis- en natuurkunde in Utrecht en deed vervolgens 13 jaar onderzoek in de natuurkunde, in Nederland, de Verenigde Staten en Zweden. Daarna ging hij in de politiek. In 1971 kwam hij voor D'66 in de Tweede Kamer. Twee jaar later werd hij voorzitter van de Tweede Kamer-fractie. Onder zijn leiding kwam D'66 uit een diep dal, en behaalde het in 1981 een grote verkiezingsoverwinning. Waarschijnlijk hebben zijn jeugdboeken bijgedragen aan de populariteit onder jongeren van D'66. Hij werd minister van Economische Zaken in het tweede en derde kabinet-Van Agt. Na de verkiezingsnederlaag van D'66 in 1982 verliet hij de politiek en ging in Parijs als secretaris-generaal van de Conferentie van Europese transportministers werken. In 1991 werd hij Commissaris van de Koningin in Gelderland. Eind 1996 ging hij met pensioen, maar van 1999 tot en met 2003 zat hij in de Eerste Kamer. Jan Terlouw is getrouwd en heeft een zoon en drie dochters.<br />Samen met zijn dochter Sanne schrijft Jan Terlouw detectives.</span>
